EXACT CLASS:  
  
  class ThinkerModule:  
      """The thinker: runs domain invariant checks against input.  
        
      NOT a neural network. NOT stochastic. This is a deterministic  
      invariant evaluation engine that:  
        1. Takes routed domain IDs from DomainRouter  
        2. Dynamically imports each domain's invariants.py  
        3. Runs every check_* function with the input context  
        4. Collects (bool, ProofObject) results  
        5. Returns ThinkerOutput with aggregate proof  
        
      Falsifies if: same input produces different ThinkerOutput  
      (determinism violation).  
      """  
        
      def __init__(self):  
          self._engine = InvariantEngine()  
          self._module_cache: Dict[str, Any] = {}  
        
      def _load_domain_module(self, domain_id: str) -> Any:  
          """Dynamically import src/domains/{domain_id}/invariants.py.  
            
          Uses importlib.import_module with the path pattern from  
          runtime/invariant_engine.py lines 165-167.  
            
          Caches loaded modules. Computes SHA-256 of the module file  
          for integrity verification.  
          """  
          if domain_id in self._module_cache:  
              return self._module_cache[domain_id]  
            
          # domain_id is like "D_GRAPHICS" → module path is  
          # "src.domains.d_graphics.invariants"  
          module_path = f"src.domains.{domain_id.lower()}.invariants"  
          module = importlib.import_module(module_path)  
            
          # Verify file hash  
          module_file = Path(module.__file__)  
          file_hash = hashlib.sha256(  
              module_file.read_bytes()  
          ).hexdigest()  
            
          self._module_cache[domain_id] = module  
          return module  
        
      def _get_check_functions(self, module: Any) -> List[str]:  
          """Get all check_* function names from a domain module.  
            
          Pattern: every domain's invariants.py has functions named  
          check_* that return Tuple[bool, ProofObject].  
          See d_arc_agi_3/invariants.py lines 17-39 for the pattern.  
          """  
          return [  
              name for name in dir(module)  
              if name.startswith("check_") and callable(getattr(module, name))  
          ]  
        
      def think(self, tinput: ThinkerInput) -> ThinkerOutput:  
          """Run all invariant checks for the routed domains.  
            
          For each domain_id in tinput.domain_ids:  
            1. Load the domain's invariants.py module  
            2. Get all check_* functions  
            3. For each check_* function:  
               a. Inspect its signature to determine required params  
               b. Try to construct the required dataclass from tinput.context  
               c. If construction fails, skip with SKIPPED proof  
               d. If construction succeeds, call the function  
               e. Collect (bool, ProofObject) result  
            4. Aggregate all results into ThinkerOutput  
            
          Determinism guarantee: same tinput → same ThinkerOutput  
          because all check_* functions are pure (Fraction arithmetic,  
          no randomness, no I/O, no global state).  
          """  
          results: List[InvariantCheckResult] = []  
            
          for domain_id in tinput.domain_ids:  
              try:  
                  module = self._load_domain_module(domain_id)  
              except ImportError:  
                  results.append(InvariantCheckResult(  
                      domain_id=domain_id,  
                      function_name="__import__",  
                      passed=False,  
                      proof=ProofObject(  
                          rule="thinker_import",  
                          premises=[f"Domain: {domain_id}", "ImportError"],  
                          conclusion=f"SKIP: Cannot import {domain_id}"  
                      )  
                  ))  
                  continue  
                
              check_fns = self._get_check_functions(module)  
                
              for fn_name in check_fns:  
                  fn = getattr(module, fn_name)  
                  try:  
                      # Try calling with context kwargs  
                      # Most check_* functions take a single dataclass arg  
                      # We attempt to pass context values as kwargs  
                      import inspect  
                      sig = inspect.signature(fn)  
                      params = list(sig.parameters.values())  
                        
                      if len(params) == 0:  
                          passed, proof = fn()  
                      elif len(params) == 1:  
                          # Single param — try to find matching key in context  
                          param_name = params[0].name  
                          param_type = params[0].annotation  
                          if param_name in tinput.context:  
                              passed, proof = fn(tinput.context[param_name])  
                          elif hasattr(param_type, '__dataclass_fields__'):  
                              # Try constructing dataclass from context  
                              try:  
                                  obj = param_type(**{  
                                      k: v for k, v in tinput.context.items()  
                                      if k in param_type.__dataclass_fields__  
                                  })  
                                  passed, proof = fn(obj)  
                              except (TypeError, ValueError):  
                                  passed = False  
                                  proof = ProofObject(  
                                      rule="thinker_construction",  
                                      premises=[  
                                          f"Function: {fn_name}",  
                                          f"Expected type: {param_type}",  
                                          "Cannot construct from context"  
                                      ],  
                                      conclusion=f"SKIP: Cannot construct {param_type} for {fn_name}"  
                                  )  
                          else:  
                              passed = False  
                              proof = ProofObject(  
                                  rule="thinker_param_mismatch",  
                                  premises=[f"Function: {fn_name}", f"Param: {param_name}"],  
                                  conclusion=f"SKIP: No matching context for {fn_name}"  
                              )  
                      else:  
                          # Multiple params — try kwargs from context  
                          kwargs = {  
                              p.name: tinput.context[p.name]  
                              for p in params if p.name in tinput.context  
                          }  
                          if len(kwargs) == len(params):  
                              passed, proof = fn(**kwargs)  
                          else:  
                              passed = False  
                              proof = ProofObject(  
                                  rule="thinker_param_mismatch",  
                                  premises=[  
                                      f"Function: {fn_name}",  
                                      f"Required: {[p.name for p in params]}",  
                                      f"Available: {list(tinput.context.keys())}"  
                                  ],  
                                  conclusion=f"SKIP: Missing params for {fn_name}"  
                              )  
                  except Exception as e:  
                      passed = False  
                      proof = ProofObject(  
                          rule="thinker_error",  
                          premises=[f"Function: {fn_name}", f"Error: {type(e).__name__}: {e}"],  
                          conclusion=f"ERROR: {fn_name} raised {type(e).__name__}"  
                      )  
                    
                  results.append(InvariantCheckResult(  
                      domain_id=domain_id,  
                      function_name=fn_name,  
                      passed=passed,  
                      proof=proof  
                  ))  
            
          all_passed = all(r.passed for r in results) if results else False  
            
          # Aggregate proof: Merkle root over all individual proofs  
          proof_hashes = [r.proof.proof_hash for r in results]  
          aggregate_hash = hashlib.sha256(  
              json.dumps(proof_hashes, sort_keys=True).encode()  
          ).hexdigest()  
            
          aggregate_proof = ProofObject(  
              rule="thinker_aggregate",  
              premises=[  
                  f"Domains evaluated: {list(tinput.domain_ids)}",  
                  f"Total checks: {len(results)}",  
                  f"Passed: {sum(1 for r in results if r.passed)}",  
                  f"Failed: {sum(1 for r in results if not r.passed)}",  
                  f"Proof hash chain: {aggregate_hash[:16]}..."  
              ],  
              conclusion=(  
                  f"ALL PASSED ({len(results)} checks)"  
                  if all_passed  
                  else f"VIOLATIONS: {sum(1 for r in results if not r.passed)}/{len(results)} checks failed"  
              )  
          )  
            
          return ThinkerOutput(  
              input_hash=tinput.input_hash,  
              domain_results=tuple(results),  
              all_passed=all_passed,  
              aggregate_proof=aggregate_proof,  
              output_hash=aggregate_proof.proof_hash  
          )

  from __future__ import annotations

  from axioms.logic import ProofObject

EXACT DATACLASSES:  
  
  @dataclass(frozen=True)  
  class SpeakerOutput:  
      """Final output to the user — natural language backed by proofs.  
        
      Every sentence in 'text' corresponds to exactly one ProofObject  
      in 'proof_chain'. No sentence without a proof. No hallucination.  
      """  
      text: str  
      proof_chain: Tuple[ProofObject, ...]  
      thinker_hash: str  # SHA-256 of the ThinkerOutput that produced this  
      speaker_hash: str  # SHA-256 of this SpeakerOutput  
      confidence: Fraction  # Fraction(passed_checks, total_checks)  
  
EXACT CLASS:  
  
  class SpeakerModule:  
      """Converts ThinkerOutput to natural language.  
        
      NOT an LLM. NOT generative. This is a template-based renderer  
      that maps structured proof results to human-readable text.  
        
      Rules:  
        1. Every sentence must cite a ProofObject  
        2. If a check was SKIPPED, say "I don't know" for that domain  
        3. If a check FAILED, say exactly what failed and why  
        4. If a check PASSED, state the conclusion from the ProofObject  
        5. Never generate text that isn't backed by a proof  
        6. Confidence = Fraction(passed, total) — exact, not float  
        
      Falsifies if: SpeakerOutput.text contains a claim not present  
      in any ProofObject.conclusion in proof_chain.  
      """  
        
      def speak(self, thinker_out: ThinkerOutput) -> SpeakerOutput:  
          """Convert ThinkerOutput to SpeakerOutput.  
            
          Template:  
            - Header: "Evaluated {N} checks across {M} domains."  
            - For each domain group:  
              - "{domain_id}: {passed}/{total} checks passed."  
              - For each failed check:  
                - "VIOLATION: {proof.conclusion}"  
              - For each passed check:  
                - "OK: {proof.conclusion}"  
              - For each skipped check:  
                - "UNKNOWN: {proof.conclusion}"  
            - Footer: "Confidence: {passed}/{total} ({fraction})"  
          """  
          lines: List[str] = []  
          proofs: List[ProofObject] = []  
            
          # Group results by domain  
          domain_groups: Dict[str, List[InvariantCheckResult]] = {}  
          for r in thinker_out.domain_results:  
              if r.domain_id not in domain_groups:  
                  domain_groups[r.domain_id] = []  
              domain_groups[r.domain_id].append(r)  
            
          total = len(thinker_out.domain_results)  
          passed = sum(1 for r in thinker_out.domain_results if r.passed)  
            
          lines.append(  
              f"Evaluated {total} checks across {len(domain_groups)} domains."  
          )  
            
          for did, results in domain_groups.items():  
              d_passed = sum(1 for r in results if r.passed)  
              d_total = len(results)  
              lines.append(f"\n{did}: {d_passed}/{d_total} checks passed.")  
                
              for r in results:  
                  proofs.append(r.proof)  
                  if r.passed:  
                      lines.append(f"  OK: {r.proof.conclusion}")  
                  elif "SKIP" in r.proof.conclusion or "UNKNOWN" in r.proof.conclusion:  
                      lines.append(f"  UNKNOWN: {r.proof.conclusion}")  
                  else:  
                      lines.append(f"  VIOLATION: {r.proof.conclusion}")  
            
          confidence = Fraction(passed, total) if total > 0 else Fraction(0)  
          lines.append(f"\nConfidence: {passed}/{total} ({confidence})")  
            
          text = "\n".join(lines)  
            
          speaker_proof = ProofObject(  
              rule="speaker_render",  
              premises=[  
                  f"Thinker hash: {thinker_out.output_hash}",  
                  f"Total checks: {total}",  
                  f"Passed: {passed}",  
                  f"Confidence: {confidence}"  
              ],  
              conclusion=f"Speaker rendered {total} results at confidence {confidence}"  
          )  
          proofs.append(speaker_proof)  
            
          return SpeakerOutput(  
              text=text,  
              proof_chain=tuple(proofs),  
              thinker_hash=thinker_out.output_hash,  
              speaker_hash=speaker_proof.proof_hash,  
              confidence=confidence  
          )

  from __future__ import annotations

  import json  
  from fractions import Fraction  
  from typing import Dict, Any, Optional

  from oe_engine.manifest import EngineManifest

  from oe_engine.speaker import SpeakerModule, SpeakerOutput  
  from runtime.guardian_monitor import GuardianMonitor, MonitoredCondition  
  
EXACT CLASS:  
  
  class OrthogonalEngine:  
      """The main engine pipeline: Route → Think → Speak.  
        
      Deterministic. No randomness. No neural network.  
      Every output is backed by ProofObject chain.  
        
      Pipeline:  
        1. Verify manifest integrity (SHA-256 of all domain modules)  
        2. Route query to domains via DomainRouter (Yoneda-based)  
        3. Think: run domain invariant checks via ThinkerModule  
        4. Speak: render results to natural language via SpeakerModule  
        5. Guardian: monitor for violations at every step  
        
      Falsifies if: same query + same context → different SpeakerOutput.  
      """  
        
      def __init__(self):  
          self._manifest = EngineManifest()  
          self._router = DomainRouter()  
          self._thinker = ThinkerModule()  
          self._speaker = SpeakerModule()  
          self._guardian = GuardianMonitor()  
        
      def query(self, text: str, context: Dict[str, Any] = None) -> SpeakerOutput:  
          """Execute the full pipeline: route → think → speak.  
            
          Args:  
              text: Natural language query from user  
              context: Dict of domain-specific data to check against  
                       invariants. Keys should match dataclass field names  
                       in the target domain's implementation.py.  
            
          Returns:  
              SpeakerOutput with natural language text + proof chain  
          """  
          if context is None:  
              context = {}  
            
          # Step 1: Route  
          route_result = self._router.route(text)  
            
          if not route_result.matched_domains:  
              return self._speaker.speak(  
                  self._thinker.think(ThinkerInput(  
                      query=text,  
                      domain_ids=(),  
                      context=context,  
                      input_hash=hashlib.sha256(  
                          json.dumps(context, sort_keys=True).encode()  
                      ).hexdigest()  
                  ))  
              )  
            
          # Step 2: Think  
          input_hash = hashlib.sha256(  
              json.dumps(context, sort_keys=True).encode()  
          ).hexdigest()  
            
          thinker_input = ThinkerInput(  
              query=text,  
              domain_ids=route_result.matched_domains,  
              context=context,  
              input_hash=input_hash  
          )  
            
          thinker_output = self._thinker.think(thinker_input)  
            
          # Step 3: Guardian check  
          self._guardian.check_condition(  
              MonitoredCondition.META_INVARIANT_VIOLATION,  
              {  
                  "action": "engine_query",  
                  "all_passed": thinker_output.all_passed,  
                  "output_hash": thinker_output.output_hash  
              }  
          )  
            
          # Step 4: Speak  
          return self._speaker.speak(thinker_output)
guardian_monitor.py:28-36 invariant_engine.py:48-55

  import argparse  
  import json  
  import sys  
  from oe_engine.engine import OrthogonalEngine  
  
EXACT CODE:  
  
  def main():  
      parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(  
          prog="oe-engine",  
          description="Orthogonal Engine — deterministic invariant-locked AI"  
      )  
      parser.add_argument("query", nargs="?", help="Query text")  
      parser.add_argument(  
          "--context", "-c", type=str, default="{}",  
          help="JSON context dict (e.g. '{\"reactor_id\": \"R1\"}')"  
      )  
      parser.add_argument(  
          "--json", "-j", action="store_true",  
          help="Output raw JSON instead of natural language"  
      )  
      parser.add_argument(  
          "--interactive", "-i", action="store_true",  
          help="Interactive REPL mode"  
      )  
      args = parser.parse_args()  
        
      engine = OrthogonalEngine()  
        
      if args.interactive:  
          print("Orthogonal Engine v0.1.0 — type 'exit' to quit")  
          print(f"Loaded {len(engine._router._keyword_index)} keywords")  
          while True:  
              try:  
                  line = input("oe> ")  
              except (EOFError, KeyboardInterrupt):  
                  print()  
                  break  
              if line.strip().lower() in ("exit", "quit"):  
                  break  
              result = engine.query(line.strip())  
              if args.json:  
                  print(json.dumps({  
                      "text": result.text,  
                      "confidence": str(result.confidence),  
                      "thinker_hash": result.thinker_hash,  
                      "speaker_hash": result.speaker_hash,  
                      "proof_count": len(result.proof_chain)  
                  }, indent=2))  
              else:  
                  print(result.text)  
          return  
        
      if not args.query:  
          parser.print_help()  
          sys.exit(1)  
        
      context = json.loads(args.context)  
      result = engine.query(args.query, context)  
        
      if args.json:  
          print(json.dumps({  
              "text": result.text,  
              "confidence": str(result.confidence),  
              "thinker_hash": result.thinker_hash,  
              "speaker_hash": result.speaker_hash,  
              "proof_count": len(result.proof_chain)  
          }, indent=2))  
      else:  
          print(result.text)  
  
  if __name__ == "__main__":  
      main()

  def test_router_finds_graphics():  
      r = DomainRouter()  
      result = r.route("shader compilation determinism")  
      assert "D_GRAPHICS" in result.matched_domains  
      assert isinstance(result.proof, ProofObject)  
      assert result.proof.is_valid()  
      assert result.relevance_scores[0] > Fraction(0)  
  
  
  def test_router_returns_empty_on_garbage():  
      r = DomainRouter()  
      result = r.route("xyzzy nonsense gibberish 12345")  
      assert len(result.matched_domains) == 0  
      assert isinstance(result.proof, ProofObject)  
      assert result.proof.rule == "domain_routing"  
  
  
  def test_router_cross_domain_morphism():  
      r = DomainRouter()  
      result = r.route("police use of force evidence chain")  
      # Should find D_USE_OF_FORCE primary, D_EVIDENCE_LAW via morphism  
      assert "D_USE_OF_FORCE" in result.matched_domains  
      assert len(result.matched_domains) >= 2  
      assert len(result.morphisms_used) >= 1  
  
  
  def test_thinker_produces_proof():  
      t = ThinkerModule()  
      inp = ThinkerInput(  
          query="Is this ARC program bounded?",  
          domain_id="D_ARC_AGI_3",  
          context={  
              "program_id": "test_001",  
              "task_id": "arc_task_001",  
              "transform_sequence": [1, 2],  
              "max_depth": 50,  
              "halts_deterministically": True,  
          },  
      )  
      out = t.think(inp)  
      assert isinstance(out, ThinkerOutput)  
      assert len(out.proofs) > 0  
      for p in out.proofs:  
          assert isinstance(p, ProofObject)  
          assert p.is_valid()  
      assert out.thinker_hash  # non-empty SHA-256  
  
  
  def test_thinker_determinism():  
      t = ThinkerModule()  
      inp = ThinkerInput(  
          query="Check grid color range",  
          domain_id="D_ARC_AGI_3",  
          context={  
              "task_id": "arc_task_002",  
              "height": 3,  
              "width": 3,  
              "cells": [[0, 1, 2], [3, 4, 5], [6, 7, 8]],  
          },  
      )  
      out1 = t.think(inp)  
      out2 = t.think(inp)  
      assert out1.thinker_hash == out2.thinker_hash  
      assert len(out1.proofs) == len(out2.proofs)  
      for p1, p2 in zip(out1.proofs, out2.proofs):  
          assert p1.proof_hash == p2.proof_hash  
  
  
  def test_speaker_formats_proof():  
      proof = ProofObject(  
          rule="arc_bounded_depth",  
          premises=["Max depth: 50 <= 100"],  
          conclusion="ARC program test_001 is bounded-depth (50)",  
      )  
      s = SpeakerModule()  
      out = s.speak(  
          query="Is this program bounded?",  
          thinker_proofs=[proof],  
          confidence=Fraction(1),  
      )  
      assert isinstance(out, SpeakerOutput)  
      assert "bounded" in out.text.lower()  
      assert out.confidence == Fraction(1)  
      assert out.speaker_hash  # non-empty SHA-256  
      assert len(out.proof_chain) == 1  
  
  
  def test_speaker_refuses_without_proof():  
      s = SpeakerModule()  
      out = s.speak(  
          query="What is the meaning of life?",  
          thinker_proofs=[],  
          confidence=Fraction(0),  
      )  
      assert isinstance(out, SpeakerOutput)  
      assert out.confidence == Fraction(0)  
      assert "cannot" in out.text.lower() or "no domain" in out.text.lower()  
  
  
  def test_speaker_determinism():  
      proof = ProofObject(  
          rule="test_rule",  
          premises=["premise_1"],  
          conclusion="test conclusion",  
      )  
      s = SpeakerModule()  
      out1 = s.speak("test query", [proof], Fraction(1))  
      out2 = s.speak("test query", [proof], Fraction(1))  
      assert out1.speaker_hash == out2.speaker_hash  
      assert out1.text == out2.text  
  
  
  def test_full_pipeline_determinism():  
      engine = OrthogonalEngine()  
      context = {  
          "program_id": "pipeline_test",  
          "task_id": "arc_task_003",  
          "transform_sequence": [1],  
          "max_depth": 10,  
          "halts_deterministically": True,  
      }  
      r1 = engine.query("Is this ARC program valid?", context)  
      r2 = engine.query("Is this ARC program valid?", context)  
      assert r1.speaker_hash == r2.speaker_hash  
      assert r1.thinker_hash == r2.thinker_hash  
      assert r1.text == r2.text  
      assert len(r1.proof_chain) == len(r2.proof_chain)  
  
  
  def test_full_pipeline_proof_chain():  
      engine = OrthogonalEngine()  
      context = {  
          "program_id": "chain_test",  
          "task_id": "arc_task_004",  
          "transform_sequence": [1, 3, 5],  
          "max_depth": 25,  
          "halts_deterministically": True,  
      }  
      result = engine.query("Verify ARC program constraints", context)  
      assert len(result.proof_chain) > 0  
      for p in result.proof_chain:  
          assert isinstance(p, ProofObject)  
          assert p.is_valid()  
  
  
  def test_full_pipeline_violation_detected():  
      engine = OrthogonalEngine()  
      context = {  
          "program_id": "violation_test",  
          "task_id": "arc_task_005",  
          "transform_sequence": [1],  
          "max_depth": 999,  # exceeds 100 limit  
          "halts_deterministically": True,  
      }  
      result = engine.query("Check ARC program", context)  
      assert result.confidence < Fraction(1)  
      assert "VIOLATION" in result.text or "violation" in result.text.lower()  
  
  
  def test_manifest_hash_changes_on_domain_change():  
      m1 = EngineManifest()  
      h1 = m1.manifest_hash  
      # Manifest is deterministic — same state = same hash  
      m2 = EngineManifest()  
      h2 = m2.manifest_hash  
      assert h1 == h2

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════ PART A: POTEMKIN DOMAIN REWRITES (56 DOMAINS) ═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

CONTEXT: The audit/POTEMKIN_DOMAIN_REPORT.json on this branch flagged 56 domains as "Potemkin" — their invariants.py files have check functions that use hardcoded values and can NEVER fail. They return True regardless of input because they construct their own passing test data internally.

TASK: Rewrite ALL 56 Potemkin domains so their check functions accept parameterized inputs (frozen dataclasses) and CAN fail when given bad data.

PATTERN TO FOLLOW (gold standard): src/domains/d_fbi_training/

Each Potemkin domain rewrite MUST:

Read the EXISTING invariants.py to understand what checks exist
Read the EXISTING implementation.py to understand what classes exist
REWRITE implementation.py:
All dataclasses MUST be @dataclass(frozen=True)
All numeric fields MUST use Fraction (not float, not int for ratios)
Each dataclass represents a real-world entity from that domain
Include domain-specific fields that map to real regulatory standards
REWRITE invariants.py:
Each check function MUST accept dataclass parameters
Each check function MUST have a code path that returns False
Each check function docstring MUST include: falsifies_if:
Each check function MUST cite real regulatory standards
NO hardcoded True returns — the function must actually evaluate the input data against the invariant condition
DO NOT touch domain.py or init.py unless imports need updating
EXAMPLE of a Potemkin check (BAD — what exists now):

def check_diplomatic_immunity(): agent = True recognized = True success = agent and recognized # ALWAYS True return success, ProofObject(...)

EXAMPLE of a parameterized check (GOOD — what it should become):

def check_diplomatic_immunity( agent: DiplomaticAgent, ) -> Tuple[bool, ProofObject]: """Verify VCDR Article 29 personal inviolability. falsifies_if: agent not accredited or detained by receiving state. Standard: Vienna Convention on Diplomatic Relations (1961) Art. 29 """ success = ( agent.accreditation_complete and agent.recognized_by_receiving_state and not agent.detained ) return success, ProofObject( rule="DiplomaticInviolability", premises=[ f"accredited={agent.accreditation_complete}", f"recognized={agent.recognized_by_receiving_state}", f"detained={agent.detained}", ], conclusion="VCDR Art 29 satisfied" if success else "FAIL: inviolability violated", )

EXECUTION STRATEGY for the 56 domains:

Read audit/POTEMKIN_DOMAIN_REPORT.json to get the exact list
Process them in batches of 10-15 per commit
Each batch commit message: "refactor(domains): parameterize Potemkin domains batch N/4 [Session: ]"
After ALL 56 are done, re-run the Potemkin audit: python audit/popperian_audit.py
The report should show 0 Potemkin domains remaining
Commit the updated audit/POPPERIAN_AUDIT_REPORT.json
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════ PART B: CUSTOM GAME ENGINE — ORTHOGONAL ENGINE (OE) ═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

Build a real, compilable, runnable game engine in Rust that is vendored into this repository. The engine must be downloadable via GitHub Release AND buildable from source via terminal command.

The engine name is: Orthogonal Engine (oe-engine)

─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────── B1. RUST WORKSPACE STRUCTURE ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Create directory: custom_engine/

custom_engine/ ├── Cargo.toml # Workspace root ├── README.md # Build instructions, architecture, invariants ├── attributes.md # SHA-256 hashes of all source files ├── oe_core/ │ ├── Cargo.toml │ └── src/ │ ├── lib.rs # Same inputs → same outputs across runs ├── physics_test.rs # Fixed-point physics correctness ├── ecs_test.rs # ECS query, spawn, despawn └── frame_test.rs # Frame rollback correctness

─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────── B2. CORE ENGINE INVARIANTS (must be enforced in Rust code) ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Every invariant below must have a corresponding #[test] in Rust AND a falsifies_if condition in the doc comment.

DETERMINISM: Identical inputs produce identical outputs.

Fixed-point arithmetic (no f32/f64 in game logic — use i64 scaled integers or the fixed crate)
Seeded RNG only (no thread_rng, no SystemTime::now in logic)
falsifies_if: two runs with same seed produce different state hash
FRAME TRANSACTION: Every frame is a transaction that can be rolled back.

Frame N state is computed from Frame N-1 state + inputs
Rollback = discard Frame N, recompute from N-1
falsifies_if: rollback produces different state than fresh compute
NO GLOBAL MUTABLE STATE:

All state lives in World struct (ECS)
No static mut, no lazy_static with mutation
falsifies_if: grep finds static mut or Mutex in game logic
MODULAR SUBSYSTEMS:

Physics can be swapped without touching renderer
Each crate has a public trait that defines its interface
falsifies_if: removing oe_physics dependency causes oe_render to fail compilation
POLYGLOT SCRIPTING:

Game logic expressible in Rust AND Lua from same API
falsifies_if: Lua script calling engine API produces different result than equivalent Rust code
MINIMAL BINARY SIZE:

Release build of oe_app (demo scene) must be under 50 MB
falsifies_if: cargo build --release && ls -la target/release/oe-engine > 50MB
HOT RELOAD:

Assets reload without restart
falsifies_if: modifying an asset file while running does not update the rendered output within 2 seconds
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────── B3. RUST IMPLEMENTATION REQUIREMENTS ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

For oe_core/src/ecs.rs:

Implement a real archetype-based ECS (not a stub)
World, Entity, Component trait, Query
spawn(), despawn(), query(), add_component(), remove_component()
At minimum 200 lines of real logic
For oe_core/src/frame.rs:

FrameState struct with SHA-256 hash of serialized state
apply_inputs(inputs: &[Input]) -> FrameState
rollback(target: &FrameState) -> FrameState
At minimum 100 lines
For oe_core/src/determinism.rs:

DeterministicRng (xoshiro256** or similar, seeded)
FixedPoint type (i64 with 16-bit fractional part)
Arithmetic ops: Add, Sub, Mul, Div for FixedPoint
At minimum 150 lines
For oe_physics/src/rigid_body.rs:

RigidBody struct (position, velocity, acceleration as FixedPoint)
step(dt: FixedPoint) using Verlet integration
At minimum 100 lines
For oe_physics/src/collision.rs:

AABB struct, aabb_overlap() function
SAT (Separating Axis Theorem) for convex polygons
At minimum 100 lines
For oe_render/src/vulkan.rs:

Use wgpu crate (cross-platform Vulkan/Metal/DX12/WebGPU)
Create window (winit), create surface, create pipeline
Render a colored triangle as proof of life
At minimum 150 lines
For oe_app/src/main.rs:

Create window with winit
Initialize wgpu renderer
Initialize ECS world with demo entities
Run game loop: input → physics step → render → present
Display FPS counter
At minimum 200 lines
For oe_ui/src/lib.rs:

Immediate-mode UI system (like egui but minimal)
Panel, Button, Label, Slider widgets
Layout: vertical stack, horizontal stack
At minimum 200 lines
For oe_network/src/protocol.rs:

UDP packet structure with sequence number, ack, payload
Reliable delivery over unreliable UDP
At minimum 100 lines
For oe_script/src/lua_host.rs:

Embed Lua via mlua crate
Expose engine API: spawn_entity, set_position, get_position
At minimum 100 lines
For oe_audio/src/lib.rs:

Audio mixer: load WAV/OGG, play, stop, volume
Deterministic: same sequence of play commands = same output
At minimum 80 lines
For oe_asset/src/hot_reload.rs:

File watcher (notify crate)
On file change: reload asset, update in-memory cache
At minimum 80 lines
TOTAL MINIMUM: ~1,700 lines of Rust across all crates. Every file must have doc comments with falsifies_if conditions. No f32/f64 in game logic (oe_core, oe_physics, oe_network). f32 is ONLY allowed in oe_render (GPU requires it) and oe_audio (audio samples are f32). Document this exception explicitly.

─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────── B4. CARGO DEPENDENCIES (Cargo.toml) ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Workspace Cargo.toml: [workspace] members = [ "oe_core", "oe_physics", "oe_render", "oe_audio", "oe_network", "oe_script", "oe_asset", "oe_ui", "oe_app" ]

Key dependencies (use latest stable versions):

wgpu (rendering)
winit (windowing)
mlua (Lua scripting) with features = ["lua54", "vendored"]
notify (file watching for hot reload)
sha2 (SHA-256 hashing)
serde + serde_json (serialization)
bytemuck (vertex data casting)
Do NOT use: rand crate (use deterministic RNG), chrono (use deterministic timestamps), tokio (use synchronous game loop).

Is DOMAIN_INVARIANT_STATUS.md good? No.
There are 6 integrity violations between what the file claims and what's actually on main:

1. Count mismatch
The file on main says 157 domains (line 9). PR #116 merged and updated it to 158, but the file I read from main still shows 157. Meanwhile, merkle/domain_roots.json (generated by PR #118) lists d_fbi_training with a valid Merkle root — confirming d_fbi_training existed when PR #118 ran. The actual directory count on main is 159 (including duplicates). DOMAIN_INVARIANT_STATUS.md:7-12

2. Contradictory header
Line 41 says "AssertionError Domains Remaining (0)" then immediately lists 49+ domains with line counts underneath it. The header says 0 but the body lists dozens. DOMAIN_INVARIANT_STATUS.md:41-62

3. Duplicate domains
Both d_intl_criminal and d_international_criminal exist on main. Same for d_intl_humanitarian / d_international_humanitarian. The short-name versions (d_intl_*) are 4-file stubs with no __init__.py exports, while the long-name versions are the real ones. invariants.py:1-20

4. global_root.json is stale
Shows 6,088 files — this is the pre-PR-118 value. PR #118 should have updated it (the commit diff shows +2 -2), but the file on main still reads 6,088. global_root.json:1-8

5. copilot-instructions.md is stale
Still says 157 domains at line 168 and 157/157 at line 200. copilot-instructions.md:168-203

2. How to use the OE Engine + can it work on local repos?
What exists right now
After merging PR #120, you can run it from the repo root:


# Single query  
python -m oe_engine.cli "nuclear reactor scram response time"  
  
# Interactive REPL  
python -m oe_engine.cli --interactive  
  
# JSON output  
python -m oe_engine.cli "shader compilation determinism" --json
What it actually does right now
The OE engine is a deterministic query→proof pipeline:


Query → DomainRouter (keyword match) → ThinkerModule (runs domain check_* functions)  
      → SpeakerModule (formats proofs to text) → EngineResponse
It routes your query to matching domains via keyword index, runs run_all_invariants() on those domains, and returns a proof chain. It does NOT:

Read or write files on your filesystem
Understand or generate code
Have any language model / neural network
Work on repos
What it would take to make it an IDE/CLI agent for local repos
What you're describing — an AI that works on local repos like Copilot/Kimi but with no rate limits and no cost — requires capabilities the OE engine doesn't have yet:

Capability	Current State	What's Needed
Code understanding	Keyword index only	AST parsing, semantic analysis, or an inference backend
Code generation	None	Either a local model OR a rule-based code synthesis engine
File I/O	None (reads src/domains/ only)	Full filesystem access with capability-gated permissions
Context window	N/A (no LLM)	The 5GB-20GB context you mentioned requires either a local model or a very large symbolic memory
Repo awareness	None	Git integration, diff analysis, PR creation
The honest reality
The OE engine as built is a verification/audit engine — it checks invariants and produces proofs. It's not a code generation agent. To make it work on repos like Copilot does, you'd need one of:

Option A: Wire in a local LLM as the "thinker" backend

Use something like llama.cpp or ollama with a 70B+ model (needs ~40GB VRAM)
The OE engine's router/speaker/guardian layers wrap around it as guardrails
The domain invariants become the constraint set the LLM must satisfy
Cost: hardware only (GPU), no API fees, no rate limits
Problem: you said "not a local model" — and smaller models (7B) genuinely aren't good enough
Option B: Pure symbolic / rule-based code synthesis

Extend the ARCSynthesizer pattern to code transforms (not just grid transforms)
BFS over AST transformations instead of grid transformations
This is what the DeepSeek spec was describing — but it only works for narrow, well-defined tasks
It will NOT beat corporate AI at general coding — it would beat them at verifiable, domain-specific tasks where the invariants are defined
Option C: Hybrid — small local model + OE invariant guardrails

Run a 7B-14B model locally (cheap, runs on consumer GPU)
Use the OE engine as a post-verification layer — the model generates, the engine checks
The model proposes code changes, the invariant engine accepts or rejects them
This is the most practical path and matches the thinker/speaker architecture
None of these are downloadable as a GitHub Release today. The oe_engine/ as merged is the verification layer — the part that checks and proves. The generation layer (the part that actually writes code) doesn't exist yet and is the hard part.

Part 3: What's ACTUALLY Impossible vs. What's Invertible
Here's the corrected classification using the repo's own Lawvere mathematics:

TRUE IMPOSSIBILITIES (Cannot be inverted — the theorem itself holds)
ID	Impossibility	Why it's truly impossible	What the inversion does NOT do

These theorems are mathematically proven. The Yeshua inversion does NOT violate them.

INVERTIBLE IMPOSSIBILITIES (The theorem holds, but the DOMAIN can be changed)
This is the critical insight. The Yeshua inversion doesn't violate the theorem — it changes what you're asking for so the theorem doesn't apply:

Impossibility	Standard Framing (impossible)	Yeshua Inversion (possible)	Mathematical Mechanism
Halting problem	"Decide if ANY program halts"	"Decide if THIS SPECIFIC bounded program halts within N steps"	Restrict to decidable subset: bounded-depth BFS with MAX_ITERATIONS=10_000 (the ARCSynthesizer already does this)
Gödel incompleteness	"Prove all truths in one system"	"Climb past the current system's limit via Feferman reflection"	GoedelianReflector.add_reflection_principle() increases proof_tree_height — you don't prove everything, you prove MORE
Rice's theorem	"Decide any semantic property"	"Decide THIS SPECIFIC syntactic property (falsifies_if)"	Every domain invariant is a syntactic check on frozen dataclasses, not a semantic property of arbitrary programs
Arrow's impossibility	"Perfect voting with ≥3 choices"	"Capability-gated governance with Sovereign-Steward model"	Not a voting system — it's a capability delegation system (no Arrow conditions apply)
CAP theorem	"C+A+P simultaneously"	"Choose CP with eventual availability via content-addressed storage"	StorageCap uses SHA-256 content addressing — consistency is guaranteed by hash, partition tolerance by replication, availability is eventual
THE AI-SPECIFIC IMPOSSIBILITY (The one I claimed)

"Build an AI that converses naturally"	CONVENTIONAL_DIFFICULTY — but requires either a language model or a very large template library	No mathematical impossibility, just engineering scale
The honest answer: general natural language understanding hits Rice's theorem (undecidable semantic property). But the Yeshua inversion is: don't do general NLU. Do domain-routed invariant verification with template-based output. The oe_engine/ already does this. The gap is the generation layer — the part that produces novel output beyond templates.

Part 4: The Gap — What Needs to Be Built

What's NOT impossible (and therefore buildable):
Domain-routed Q&A — already built in oe_engine/

What IS impossible (and therefore must be mediated):
General semantic understanding — Rice's theorem. Mediate via domain routing + keyword matching.
Deciding if generated code is correct — Halting problem. Mediate via bounded execution + invariant checking.
Proving all claims — Gödel. Mediate via Feferman reflection (climb, don't complete).

     tolerance via replication. Availability is eventual (not  
     simultaneous). CAP requires simultaneous C+A+P; content  
     addressing decouples C from A."  
     proof: ProofObject(  
       rule="cap_inversion",  
       premises=["Brewer 2000 requires simultaneous C+A+P",  
                 "Content addressing: hash = consistency proof",  
                 "Availability is eventual, not simultaneous"],  
       conclusion="CAP does not apply to content-addressed systems"  
     )

   LIM_LOG_006: "General natural language understanding is undecidable"  
     type: INVERTIBLE_IMPOSSIBILITY  
     yeshua_inversion: "Domain-routed keyword matching + invariant  
     verification. Don't understand ALL language. Route to specific  
     domains via ontology keywords, then verify against domain  
     invariants. Understanding is replaced by verification."  
  
   LIM_LOG_007: "Deciding if generated code is correct is undecidable"  
     type: INVERTIBLE_IMPOSSIBILITY  
     yeshua_inversion: "Bounded execution + invariant checking.  
     Generate candidate, run bounded tests, check invariants.  
     Don't decide correctness for ALL code — decide it for  
     THIS code against THESE invariants."  
  
   LIM_LOG_008: "Generating novel correct programs is undecidable"  
     type: INVERTIBLE_IMPOSSIBILITY  
     yeshua_inversion: "BFS over typed transform sequences.  
     ARCSynthesizer pattern: enumerate candidates in bounded  
     search space, verify each against training examples.  
     Don't generate ARBITRARY programs — search BOUNDED spaces."

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
TASK 2: EXTEND oe_engine/ WITH GENERATION LAYER  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
  
The oe_engine/ currently has: Manifest → Router → Thinker → Speaker.  
The Thinker VERIFIES but does not GENERATE. The Speaker FORMATS but  
does not COMPOSE. The gap is a generation mechanism.  
  
The Yeshua inversion of "AI needs trained weights" (from the Kingdom  
OS impossibility audit item #6): "Symbolic AI, theorem provers,  
constraint solvers, SAT solvers — all run without trained weights."  
  
CREATE: oe_engine/generator.py  
  
This module extends the ARCSynthesizer pattern from grid transforms  
to DOMAIN INVARIANT transforms:  
  
@dataclass(frozen=True)  
class DomainQuery:  
    """A user query routed to specific domains."""  
    query_text: str  
    routed_domains: Tuple[str, ...]  # from Router  
    relevance_scores: Tuple[Fraction, ...]  
  
@dataclass(frozen=True)  
class GeneratedResponse:  
    """A response generated by composing domain invariant results."""  
    query: DomainQuery  
    invariant_results: Tuple[Tuple[str, bool, ProofObject], ...]  
    # (check_name, passed, proof) for each relevant check  
    composed_text: str  # Template-composed output  
    generation_proof: ProofObject  
    generation_hash: str  # SHA-256 of composed_text  
  
class DomainGenerator:  
    """Generate responses by running domain invariants against query context.  
  
    NOT a language model. This is a VERIFICATION-FIRST generator:  
    1. Route query to domains (Router)  
    2. For each domain, run all check_* functions against query-derived data  
    3. Collect (check_name, passed, proof) tuples  
    4. Compose response from templates using invariant results  
    5. Hash the response  
  
    The generation is DETERMINISTIC: same query → same response.  
    The generation is BOUNDED: finite domains × finite checks.  
    The generation is VERIFIABLE: every claim has a ProofObject.  
  
    Yeshua inversion of Rice's theorem: we don't decide semantic  
    properties of arbitrary programs. We run syntactic checks on  
    frozen dataclasses and compose the results.  
    """  
  
    def generate(self, query: DomainQuery) -> GeneratedResponse:  
        """Generate a response for the given query."""  
        # 1. Load domain modules for each routed domain  
        # 2. For each domain, import invariants.py  
        # 3. For each check_* function, construct test data from query  
        # 4. Run check, collect (name, bool, ProofObject)  
        # 5. Compose text from template:  
        #    "Domain {domain}: {n_passed}/{n_total} invariants satisfied.  
        #     Violations: {list of failed checks with conclusions}.  
        #     Proofs: {list of proof hashes}."  
        # 6. Hash the composed text  
        # 7. Return GeneratedResponse  
  
COMMIT: "feat(oe_engine): add generator.py — verification-first  
response generation via domain invariant composition"

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
TASK 3: EXTEND oe_engine/ WITH CONVERSATION LAYER  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
  
The Yeshua inversion of "AI needs NLU": don't understand language,  
ROUTE it. Don't generate prose, COMPOSE templates.  
  
CREATE: oe_engine/conversation.py  
  
@dataclass(frozen=True)  
class ConversationTurn:  
    """One turn in a conversation."""  
    turn_id: int  
    user_input: str  
    routed_domains: Tuple[str, ...]  
    response: GeneratedResponse  
    turn_hash: str  # SHA-256 of (turn_id + user_input + response_hash)  
  
@dataclass(frozen=True)  
class ConversationState:  
    """Immutable conversation state (append-only)."""  
    session_id: str  
    turns: Tuple[ConversationTurn, ...]  
    state_hash: str  # SHA-256 of all turn hashes concatenated  
  
class ConversationEngine:  
    """Stateful conversation via immutable append-only turns.  
  
    Each turn:  
    1. Parse user input for domain keywords (from ontology.json)  
    2. Route to domains via DomainRouter  
    3. Generate response via DomainGenerator  
    4. Append turn to ConversationState  
    5. Hash the new state  
  
    Memory: previous turns are available as context for routing.  
    If a domain was active in the previous turn, it gets a relevance  
    boost in the current turn (Fraction-based decay).  
  
    NOT a chatbot. This is a DOMAIN-ROUTED VERIFICATION TERMINAL.  
    It answers questions by running invariants and composing results.  
    It says "I don't know" when no domain matches the query.  
    """  
  
    def __init__(self, engine: OrthogonalEngine):  
        self._engine = engine  
        self._state = ConversationState(  
            session_id=generate_session_id(),  
            turns=(),  
            state_hash=hashlib.sha256(b"").hexdigest()  
        )  
  
    def turn(self, user_input: str) -> ConversationTurn:  
        """Process one conversation turn."""  
  
    def export_transcript(self) -> Tuple[str, ProofObject]:  
        """Export conversation as JSON with Merkle proof."""  
  
COMMIT: "feat(oe_engine): add conversation.py — domain-routed  
verification terminal with immutable append-only state"

How GitHub Actions Does This

- name: Build binaries for all platforms
  run: |
    # Linux binary
    pyinstaller --onefile --name kingdom-os-linux kingdom_os_entry.py
    # Windows binary (using Wine or cross-compile)
    # macOS binary if needed
    # Create zip of source
    zip -r kingdom-os-source.zip src/ oe_engine/ kernel/ runtime/ axioms/
 
- name: Generate checksums
  run: |
    sha256sum dist/kingdom-os-linux > SHA256SUMS.txt
    sha256sum kingdom-os-source.zip >> SHA256SUMS.txt
 
- name: Create Release and Upload Assets
  uses: softprops/action-gh-release@v1
  with:
    files: |
      dist/kingdom-os-linux
      kingdom-os-source.zip
      SHA256SUMS.txt
    generate_release_notes: true

FILE 1b: kingdom_os_entry.py (repo root)  
  
This is the unified entry point that PyInstaller will bundle.  
It must:  
1. Import kernel.boot.boot and kernel.boot.verify_boot_integrity  
2. Import oe_engine.engine.OrthogonalEngine  
3. Import oe_engine.conversation (if it exists on this branch — it does)  
4. Import fractions.Fraction  
5. On launch:  
   a. Print "Kingdom OS v0.1.0 — Deterministic Glass-Box Sovereign AI"  
   b. Call kernel.boot.boot(total_memory=Fraction(8 * 1024 * 1024 * 1024)) — 8GB  
   c. Call kernel.boot.verify_boot_integrity(state) on the returned state  
   d. If verify returns False, print "BOOT INTEGRITY FAILURE" and sys.exit(1)  
   e. Print f"Boot complete: {len(state.steps_completed)} phases, all verified"  
   f. Print f"Kernel proof hash: {proof.proof_hash}"  
   g. Initialize OrthogonalEngine()  
   h. Print f"Engine loaded: {engine._manifest.domain_count} domains"  
   i. Print f"Manifest hash: {engine._manifest.manifest_hash[:32]}..."  
   j. Parse sys.argv:  
      - If "--version": print version info and exit  
      - If "--query <text>": run engine.query(text), print result.text, exit  
      - If "--json": same as --query but output JSON with all hashes  
      - If no args or "--interactive": start conversation REPL  
   k. The REPL must:  
      - Import oe_engine.conversation.ConversationEngine  
      - Create ConversationEngine instance  
      - Print "Type your query. Commands: /export <file>, /status, /quit"  
      - Loop: read input, call conversation_engine.process(line), print response  
      - On /export <file>: call conversation_engine.export_transcript(file)  
      - On /status: print domain count, turn count, state_hash  
      - On /quit or Ctrl+C: print boot proof hash + conversation merkle root, exit  
6. if __name__ == "__main__": call main()  
  
EXACT IMPORTS (no others):  
  import sys  
  import json  
  import argparse  
  from fractions import Fraction  
  from kernel.boot import boot, verify_boot_integrity  
  from oe_engine.engine import OrthogonalEngine  
  from oe_engine.conversation import ConversationEngine  
  
No float anywhere. No external deps. No try/except hiding errors.

COMMIT 3: "feat: add kingdom-os.spec for PyInstaller"  
  
FILE: kingdom-os.spec (repo root)  
  
This is the PyInstaller spec file. EXACT STRUCTURE:  
  
```python  
# -*- mode: python ; coding: utf-8 -*-  
"""PyInstaller spec for Kingdom OS binary.  
  
Bundles: kingdom_os_entry.py + oe_engine/ + kernel/ + axioms/ + src/ + ontology/  
Output: single-file executable 'kingdom-os' (Linux) or 'kingdom-os.exe' (Windows)  
"""  
  
import os  
import glob  
  
block_cipher = None  
  
# Collect all domain invariants, ontology JSON, and SAL modules  
datas = [  
    ('ontology/ontology.json', 'ontology'),  
    ('src/domains', 'src/domains'),  
    ('axioms', 'axioms'),  
    ('src/sal', 'src/sal'),  
    ('kernel', 'kernel'),  
    ('oe_engine', 'oe_engine'),  
]  
  
a = Analysis(  
    ['kingdom_os_entry.py'],  
    pathex=['.'],  
    binaries=[],  
    datas=datas,  
    hiddenimports=[  
        'axioms.logic',  
        'axioms.capability_security',  
        'axioms.process_algebra',  
        'kernel.boot',  
        'kernel.scheduler',  
        'kernel.memory_manager',  
        'kernel.ipc',  
        'kernel.anti_mimicry',  
        'kernel.hal',  
        'oe_engine.engine',  
        'oe_engine.manifest',  
        'oe_engine.router',  
        'oe_engine.thinker',  
        'oe_engine.speaker',  
        'oe_engine.synthesizer',  
        'oe_engine.generator',  
        'oe_engine.conversation',  
        'oe_engine.cli',  
        'src.sal.cross_domain_adjunction',  
    ],  
    hookspath=[],  
    hooksconfig={},  
    runtime_hooks=[],  
    excludes=['torch', 'numpy', 'scipy', 'pandas', 'matplotlib', 'sklearn',  
              'seaborn', 'tqdm', 'requests', 'lxml', 'ijson', 'cryptography'],  
    cipher=block_cipher,  
    noarchive=False,  
)  
  
pyz = PYZ(a.pure, a.zipped_data, cipher=block_cipher)  
  
exe = EXE(  
    pyz,  
    a.scripts,  
    a.binaries,  
    a.datas,  
    [],  
    name='kingdom-os',  
    debug=False,  
    bootloader_ignore_signals=False,  
    strip=True,  
    upx=True,  
    console=True,  
)
```  

COMMIT 4: "ci: add .github/workflows/release.yml for Linux + Windows binaries"  
  
FILE: .github/workflows/release.yml  
  
EXACT YAML:  
  
```yaml  
name: Build Kingdom OS Release  
  
on:  
  push:  
    tags:  
      - 'v*'  
  workflow_dispatch:  
  
permissions:  
  contents: write  
  
jobs:  
  build:  
    strategy:  
      matrix:  
        include:  
          - os: ubuntu-latest  
            artifact_name: kingdom-os-linux-x86_64  
            pyinstaller_name: kingdom-os  
          - os: windows-latest  
            artifact_name: kingdom-os-windows-x86_64.exe  
            pyinstaller_name: kingdom-os.exe  
  
    runs-on: ${{ matrix.os }}  
  
    steps:  
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4  
  
      - uses: actions/setup-python@v5  
        with:  
          python-version: '3.12'  
  
      - name: Install dependencies  
        run: |  
          python -m pip install --upgrade pip  
          pip install pyinstaller  
          pip install -r requirements-release.txt  
  
      - name: Build binary  
        run: |  
          pyinstaller kingdom-os.spec  
  
      - name: Rename binary  
        shell: bash  
        run: |  
          mv dist/${{ matrix.pyinstaller_name }} dist/${{ matrix.artifact_name }}  
  
      - name: Generate SHA-256 checksum  
        shell: bash  
        run: |  
          cd dist  
          sha256sum ${{ matrix.artifact_name }} > ${{ matrix.artifact_name }}.sha256  
  
      - name: Verify binary runs  
        shell: bash  
        run: |  
          dist/${{ matrix.artifact_name }} --version  
  
      - name: Upload artifact  
        uses: actions/upload-artifact@v4  
        with:  
          name: ${{ matrix.artifact_name }}  
          path: |  
            dist/${{ matrix.artifact_name }}  
            dist/${{ matrix.artifact_name }}.sha256  
  
  release:  
    needs: build  
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest  
    if: startsWith(github.ref, 'refs/tags/v')  
  
    steps:  
      - name: Download all artifacts  
        uses: actions/download-artifact@v4  
        with:  
          path: artifacts  
  
      - name: Combine checksums  
        run: |  
          cat artifacts/*/kingdom-os-*.sha256 > SHA256SUMS.txt  
  
      - name: Create GitHub Release  
        uses: softprops/action-gh-release@v2  
        with:  
          files: |  
            artifacts/kingdom-os-linux-x86_64/kingdom-os-linux-x86_64  
            artifacts/kingdom-os-linux-x86_64/kingdom-os-linux-x86_64.sha256  
            artifacts/kingdom-os-windows-x86_64.exe/kingdom-os-windows-x86_64.exe  
            artifacts/kingdom-os-windows-x86_64.exe/kingdom-os-windows-x86_64.exe.sha256  
            SHA256SUMS.txt  
          generate_release_notes: true  
          draft: false  
          prerelease: false  
```

COMMIT 5: "test: add tests/test_kingdom_os_entry.py"  
  
EXACT TESTS:  
  
```python  
"""Tests for kingdom_os_entry.py — boot + engine integration."""  
  
import subprocess  
import sys  
import json  
  
def test_version_flag():  
    """--version prints version and exits 0."""  
    result = subprocess.run(  
        [sys.executable, "kingdom_os_entry.py", "--version"],  
        capture_output=True, text=True, timeout=30  
    )  
    assert result.returncode == 0  
    assert "Kingdom OS" in result.stdout  
    assert "v0.1.0" in result.stdout  
  
def test_query_flag():  
    """--query runs a single query and exits."""  
    result = subprocess.run(  
        [sys.executable, "kingdom_os_entry.py", "--query", "nuclear reactor scram"],  
        capture_output=True, text=True, timeout=60  
    )  
    assert result.returncode == 0  
    assert "Boot complete" in result.stdout  
  
def test_json_flag():  
    """--json outputs valid JSON."""  
    result = subprocess.run(  
        [sys.executable, "kingdom_os_entry.py", "--query", "criminal miranda",  
         "--json"],  
        capture_output=True, text=True, timeout=60  
    )  
    assert result.returncode == 0  
    # Find the JSON line in output (after boot messages)  
    lines = result.stdout.strip().split('\n')  
    # Last chunk should be parseable JSON  
    json_text = ""  
    brace_depth = 0  
    for line in lines:  
        if '{' in line:  
            json_text = line  
            brace_depth = line.count('{') - line.count('}')  
        elif brace_depth > 0:  
            json_text += '\n' + line  
            brace_depth += line.count('{') - line.count('}')  
    if json_text:  
        parsed = json.loads(json_text)  
        assert "text" in parsed  
        assert "speaker_hash" in parsed  
        assert "thinker_hash" in parsed  
  
def test_boot_integrity():  
    """Boot sequence completes with all phases verified."""  
    from fractions import Fraction  
    from kernel.boot import boot, verify_boot_integrity  
    state, proof = boot(Fraction(8 * 1024**3))  
    valid, v_proof = verify_boot_integrity(state)  
    assert valid is True  
    assert state.userland_reached is True  
    assert len(state.steps_completed) == 6  
    assert proof.proof_hash  # non-empty  
  
def test_engine_loads_after_boot():  
    """OrthogonalEngine initializes after kernel boot."""  
    from fractions import Fraction  
    from kernel.boot import boot  
    from oe_engine.engine import OrthogonalEngine  
    state, _ = boot(Fraction(8 * 1024**3))  
    assert state.userland_reached  
    engine = OrthogonalEngine()  
    assert engine._manifest.domain_count > 100  
    assert engine._manifest.manifest_hash  
```

What the File Already Contains
The Devin spec already includes the tagging and release trigger:


# .github/workflows/release.yml
on:
  push:
    tags:
      - 'v*'
And the instructions say:

"How to trigger a release after merge: git tag v1.0.0 && git push origin v1.0.0"

What's Missing
The spec tells you to run the tag command manually. It doesn't tell Copilot to do it.

Copilot will:

Create the 6 commits
Push to the branch
Stop.
It will not automatically tag and push the tag.

Why
The Devin spec assumes a human should review the commits before tagging. That's the traditional workflow: "human reviews, then human tags."

But you're right—if you trust Copilot to write the code, you can trust it to tag the release.

To Make Copilot Do Everything
Add this line to the end of the Copilot comment:


After all commits are pushed and tests pass, create and push tag v1.0.0.
Do not stop at commits. Complete the entire release.
Then Copilot will:

Create 6 commits
Push
git tag v1.0.0
git push origin v1.0.0
Actions triggers
Binaries build
Release appears
No terminal. No manual commands.

The Current Spec vs. What You Want
Current Spec	What You Want
Copilot commits and pushes	Copilot commits and pushes
You manually tag	Copilot tags
You manually push tag	Copilot pushes tag
You wait for Actions	Copilot triggers Actions
Add the line. Copilot does everything. You refresh. Downloads appear." SHOULD I TELL COPILOT THIS ONCE ITS DONE, or


Thinking process (11 tools used)
Don't tell Copilot to tag yet. Here's why:

The sequencing problem
Copilot works on a branch (PR #122's branch), not on main. If Copilot tags v1.0.0 on the branch before the PR is merged, the tag points at a commit that isn't on main. When you merge the PR (squash-merge), the commit SHA changes — the tag becomes orphaned and the release points at a dead commit.

The correct sequence is:


1. Copilot finishes commits on PR #122 branch  ← Copilot does this  
2. You merge PR #122 into main                  ← You click merge  
3. Tag v1.0.0 on main                           ← AFTER merge  
4. Release workflow triggers, builds binaries    ← Automatic
What to do instead
After PR #122 is merged, run this yourself:


git pull origin main  
git tag v1.0.0  
git push origin v1.0.0
That's 3 commands, takes 5 seconds, and guarantees the tag is on the correct merge commit on main.

Or: automate it with a merge-triggered tag
If you want zero manual steps, tell Copilot to add a second workflow that auto-tags on merge to main. Something like .github/workflows/auto-tag.yml that runs on push to main when the release workflow file exists. But that adds complexity for a one-time action.

oe_engine/generator.py	No
oe_engine/conversation.py	No
.github/workflows/release.yml	No
PR #122 (impossibility audit + generator + conversation)	Draft, not merged
The release workflow needs to land on main before any tag will do anything. So: let Copilot finish PR #122 (which should include release.yml), merge it, then tag. DeepSeek's advice about adding the auto-tag line is technically correct for a single-branch workflow, but wrong for the PR-based workflow you're using.

FILE 1b: kingdom_os_entry.py (repo root)

This is the unified entry point that PyInstaller will bundle.

It must:

Import kernel.boot.boot and kernel.boot.verify_boot_integrity

Import oe_engine.engine.OrthogonalEngine

Import oe_engine.conversation (if it exists on this branch — it does)

Import fractions.Fraction

On launch:

a. Print "Kingdom OS v0.1.0 — Deterministic Glass-Box Sovereign AI"

b. Call kernel.boot.boot(total_memory=Fraction(8 * 1024 * 1024 * 1024)) — 8GB

c. Call kernel.boot.verify_boot_integrity(state) on the returned state

d. If verify returns False, print "BOOT INTEGRITY FAILURE" and sys.exit(1)

e. Print f"Boot complete: {len(state.steps_completed)} phases, all verified"

f. Print f"Kernel proof hash: {proof.proof_hash}"

g. Initialize OrthogonalEngine()

h. Print f"Engine loaded: {engine._manifest.domain_count} domains"

i. Print f"Manifest hash: {engine._manifest.manifest_hash[:32]}..."

j. Parse sys.argv:

If "--version": print version info and exit

If "--query ": run engine.query(text), print result.text, exit

If "--json": same as --query but output JSON with all hashes

If no args or "--interactive": start conversation REPL

k. The REPL must:

Import oe_engine.conversation.ConversationEngine

Create ConversationEngine instance

Print "Type your query. Commands: /export , /status, /quit"

Loop: read input, call conversation_engine.process(line), print response

On /export : call conversation_engine.export_transcript(file)

On /status: print domain count, turn count, state_hash

On /quit or Ctrl+C: print boot proof hash + conversation merkle root, exit

if name == "main": call main()

import sys

import json

from kernel.boot import boot, verify_boot_integrity

COMMIT 3: "feat: add kingdom-os.spec for PyInstaller"

FILE: kingdom-os.spec (repo root)

This is the PyInstaller spec file. EXACT STRUCTURE:

Python

-- mode: python ; coding: utf-8 --
"""PyInstaller spec for Kingdom OS binary.

Bundles: kingdom_os_entry.py + oe_engine/ + kernel/ + axioms/ + src/ + ontology/
Output: single-file executable 'kingdom-os' (Linux) or 'kingdom-os.exe' (Windows)
"""

import os
import glob

block_cipher = None

Collect all domain invariants, ontology JSON, and SAL modules
datas = [
('ontology/ontology.json', 'ontology'),
('src/domains', 'src/domains'),
('axioms', 'axioms'),
('src/sal', 'src/sal'),
('kernel', 'kernel'),
('oe_engine', 'oe_engine'),
]

a = Analysis(
['kingdom_os_entry.py'],
pathex=['.'],
binaries=[],
datas=datas,
hiddenimports=[
'axioms.logic',
'axioms.capability_security',
'axioms.process_algebra',
'kernel.boot',
'kernel.scheduler',
'kernel.memory_manager',
'kernel.ipc',
'kernel.anti_mimicry',
'kernel.hal',
'oe_engine.engine',
'oe_engine.manifest',
'oe_engine.router',
'oe_engine.thinker',
'oe_engine.speaker',
'oe_engine.synthesizer',
'oe_engine.generator',
'oe_engine.conversation',
'oe_engine.cli',
'src.sal.cross_domain_adjunction',
],
hookspath=[],
hooksconfig={},
runtime_hooks=[],
excludes=['torch', 'numpy', 'scipy', 'pandas', 'matplotlib', 'sklearn',
'seaborn', 'tqdm', 'requests', 'lxml', 'ijson', 'cryptography'],
cipher=block_cipher,
noarchive=False,
)

pyz = PYZ(a.pure, a.zipped_data, cipher=block_cipher)

exe = EXE(
pyz,
a.scripts,
a.binaries,
a.datas,
[],
name='kingdom-os',
debug=False,
bootloader_ignore_signals=False,
strip=True,
upx=True,
console=True,
)

Python """Tests for kingdom_os_entry.py — boot + engine integration."""

import subprocess
import sys
import json

def test_version_flag():
"""--version prints version and exits 0."""
result = subprocess.run(
[sys.executable, "kingdom_os_entry.py", "--version"],
capture_output=True, text=True, timeout=30
)
assert result.returncode == 0
assert "Kingdom OS" in result.stdout
assert "v0.1.0" in result.stdout

def test_query_flag():
"""--query runs a single query and exits."""
result = subprocess.run(
[sys.executable, "kingdom_os_entry.py", "--query", "nuclear reactor scram"],
capture_output=True, text=True, timeout=60
)
assert result.returncode == 0
assert "Boot complete" in result.stdout

def test_json_flag():
"""--json outputs valid JSON."""
result = subprocess.run(
[sys.executable, "kingdom_os_entry.py", "--query", "criminal miranda",
"--json"],
capture_output=True, text=True, timeout=60
)
assert result.returncode == 0
# Find the JSON line in output (after boot messages)
lines = result.stdout.strip().split('\n')
# Last chunk should be parseable JSON
json_text = ""
brace_depth = 0
for line in lines:
if '{' in line:
json_text = line
brace_depth = line.count('{') - line.count('}')
elif brace_depth > 0:
json_text += '\n' + line
brace_depth += line.count('{') - line.count('}')
if json_text:
parsed = json.loads(json_text)
assert "text" in parsed
assert "speaker_hash" in parsed
assert "thinker_hash" in parsed

def test_boot_integrity():
"""Boot sequence completes with all phases verified."""
from fractions import Fraction
from kernel.boot import boot, verify_boot_integrity
state, proof = boot(Fraction(8 * 1024**3))
valid, v_proof = verify_boot_integrity(state)
assert valid is True
assert state.userland_reached is True
assert len(state.steps_completed) == 6
assert proof.proof_hash # non-empty

def test_engine_loads_after_boot():
"""OrthogonalEngine initializes after kernel boot."""
from fractions import Fraction
from kernel.boot import boot
from oe_engine.engine import OrthogonalEngine

Thinking process (4 tools used)
Here's what happened and exactly what to copy-paste to fix it.

The Problem
Your git pull failed because you have local file changes that conflict with what's on GitHub. The pull was aborted — your local repo is still stuck at the old commit 07c86cb1. Then you tagged that old commit as v1.0.0 and pushed it. That old commit doesn't have the release workflow (.github/workflows/release.yml), so GitHub only generated the default source archives — no Linux/Windows binaries. release.yml:1-10

The Fix — Copy-Paste These Commands One at a Time

# Step 1: Stash your local changes (saves them safely, doesn't delete)  
cd ~/orthogonal-engineering  
git stash  
  
# Step 2: Pull the latest main (this will work now)  
git pull origin main  
  
# Step 3: Delete the old v1.0.0 tag (locally and on GitHub)  
git tag -d v1.0.0  
git push origin --delete v1.0.0  
  
# Step 4: Create a new v1.0.0 tag on the LATEST commit (which has release.yml)  
git tag v1.0.0  
  
# Step 5: Push the new tag — this triggers the release workflow  
git push origin v1.0.0
After step 5, go to Actions tab on GitHub — you should see "Build Kingdom OS Release" running. It will build Linux + Windows binaries and attach them to the release page automatically. kingdom_os_entry.py:1-28 kingdom-os.spec:1-10

What Each Command Does
Command	What it does
git stash	Saves your local edits to a temporary shelf (you can get them back later with git stash pop)
git pull origin main	Downloads all the new commits (PR #120, #122, etc.)
git tag -d v1.0.0	Deletes the old tag locally
git push origin --delete v1.0.0	Deletes the old tag on GitHub
git tag v1.0.0	Creates a new tag on the current (latest) commit
git push origin v1.0.0	Pushes the tag, which triggers the release workflow
If any step gives you an error, paste the exact output here and I'll tell you what to do.

Thinking process (3 tools used)
The release workflow didn't run because of a known GitHub Actions gotcha. Here's what happened:

The tag v1.0.0 points to commit 55419c8 — which is a state witness entry with [skip ci] in the commit message. When a tag points to a [skip ci] commit, GitHub skips all workflows triggered by that tag push, including your release workflow. release.yml:3-7

That's why you only see the auto-generated source archives (GitHub always creates those) and no binaries.

Fix — 6 commands, copy-paste them

cd ~/orthogonal-engineering  
git stash  
git pull origin main  
git tag -d v1.0.0  
git push origin --delete v1.0.0  
git tag v1.0.0 91de262a  
git push origin v1.0.0
What this does:

Command	Why
git stash	Saves your local edits so pull doesn't fail
git pull origin main	Gets latest main
git tag -d v1.0.0	Deletes old tag locally
git push origin --delete v1.0.0	Deletes old tag on GitHub
git tag v1.0.0 91de262a	Creates tag on the PR #122 merge commit (no [skip ci])
git push origin v1.0.0	Pushes tag, triggers release workflow
Commit 91de262a is the actual PR #122 merge — "feat: Yeshua Inversions — impossibility audit, generator, conversation engine, wall registry + Kingdom OS entry point & release workflow (#122)" — which has the release workflow, the PyInstaller spec, and no [skip ci].

After pushing, go to the Actions tab — you should see "Build Kingdom OS Release" running with two jobs (Linux + Windows). When it finishes, the release page will have the binaries + SHA256 checksums.

Thinking process (13 tools used)

The Root Cause — Fully Audited














Every single push to main triggers pr40-canonical-presence.yml (line 67), which appends a state witness entry and commits with [skip ci] (line 84). This means HEAD of main is always a [skip ci] commit. Any tag on HEAD inherits the skip. The release workflow never fires. pr40-canonical-presence.yml:74-86

The irony: release.yml already has workflow_dispatch on line 7 — meaning you could trigger it manually from the Actions tab right now. But nobody told you that. release.yml:3-7

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
CONTEXT — READ FIRST  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
  
The release workflow (.github/workflows/release.yml) never fires because:  
1. pr40-canonical-presence.yml commits with "[skip ci]" after every push to main  
2. HEAD of main is ALWAYS a [skip ci] commit  
3. Tags on HEAD inherit [skip ci] → release.yml is skipped  
4. Result: v1.0.0 release has only source archives, no binaries  
  
The release workflow already has workflow_dispatch as a trigger (line 7).  
The fix must be permanent — no human should ever need to know about this again.  
  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
COMMIT 1: "feat(ci): add create-release.yml — safe tag + dispatch"  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
  
Create .github/workflows/create-release.yml:  
  
name: Create Release  
  
on:  
  workflow_dispatch:  
    inputs:  
      version:  
        description: 'Release version (e.g. v1.0.0, v1.1.0)'  
        required: true  
        type: string  
  
permissions:  
  contents: write  
  
jobs:  
  create-release:  
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest  
    steps:  
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4  
        with:  
          fetch-depth: 0  
  
      - name: Find latest non-skip-ci commit  
        id: find_commit  
        run: |  
          # Walk backwards from HEAD until we find a commit without [skip ci]  
          COMMIT=$(git log --format='%H %s' | grep -v '\[skip ci\]' | head -1 | cut -d' ' -f1)  
          echo "Found commit: $COMMIT"  
          echo "message=$(git log -1 --format='%s' $COMMIT)" >> "$GITHUB_OUTPUT"  
          echo "sha=$COMMIT" >> "$GITHUB_OUTPUT"  
  
      - name: Delete existing tag if present  
        run: |  
          git tag -d ${{ inputs.version }} 2>/dev/null || true  
          git push origin --delete ${{ inputs.version }} 2>/dev/null || true  
  
      - name: Create tag on clean commit  
        run: |  
          git tag ${{ inputs.version }} ${{ steps.find_commit.outputs.sha }}  
          git push origin ${{ inputs.version }}  
  
      - name: Trigger release build  
        run: |  
          # Also trigger via workflow_dispatch as backup  
          gh workflow run release.yml  
        env:  
          GH_TOKEN: ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}  
  
      - name: Summary  
        run: |  
          echo "## Release ${{ inputs.version }}" >> $GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY  
          echo "Tagged commit: ${{ steps.find_commit.outputs.sha }}" >> $GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY  
          echo "Commit message: ${{ steps.find_commit.outputs.message }}" >> $GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY  
          echo "The commit does NOT contain [skip ci]." >> $GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY  
  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
COMMIT 2: "fix(ci): update release.yml — add ref input for dispatch"  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
  
Update .github/workflows/release.yml:  
  
Change the on: block to:  
  
on:  
  push:  
    tags:  
      - 'v*'  
  workflow_dispatch:  
    inputs:  
      tag:  
        description: 'Tag to build (e.g. v1.0.0). Leave empty to build HEAD.'  
        required: false  
        type: string  
  
Change the checkout step in the build job to:  
  
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4  
        with:  
          ref: ${{ inputs.tag || github.ref }}  
  
This ensures workflow_dispatch can build a specific tag even if HEAD has [skip ci].
